        <meta property="og:url" content="https://pubs.acs.org/doi/full/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056"><meta property="og:title" content="Bilateral Interfaces in In2Se3-CoIn2-CoSe2 Heterostructures for High-Rate Reversible Sodium Storage"><meta property="og:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056/asset/images/acsnano.1c03056.social.jpeg_v03"><meta property="og:description" content="Metal selenides are considered as a group of promising candidates as the anode material for sodium-ion batteries due to their high theoretical capacity. However, the intrinsically low electrical and ionic conductivities as well as huge volume change during the charge-discharge process give rise to an inferior sodium storage capability, which severely hinders their practical application. Herein, we fabricated In2Se3/CoSe2 hollow nanorods composed of In2Se3/CoIn2/CoSe2 by growing cobalt-based zeolitic imidazolate framework ZIF-67 on the surface of indium-based metal–organic framework MIL-68, followed by in situ gaseous selenization. Because of the CoIn2 alloy phase in between In2Se3 and CoSe2, a heterostructure consisting of two alloy/selenide interfaces has been successfully constructed, offering synergistically enhanced electrical conductivity, Na diffusion process, and structural stability, in comparison to the single CoIn2-free interface with only two metal selenides. As expected, this nanoconstruction delivers a high reversible capacity of 297.5 and 205.5 mAh g–1 at 5 and 10 A g–1 after 2000 cycles, respectively, and a superior rate performance of 371.6 mAh g–1 at even 20 A g–1."><meta property="og:type" content="Article"><meta property="og:site_name" content="ACS Publications"><meta name="twitter:card" content="summary_large_image"><meta name="twitter:site" content="@ACSPublications"><meta name="twitter:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056/asset/images/acsnano.1c03056.social.jpeg_v03">

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/wro/1122814~thiss-ds.js" async="" nonce="93188be17fb9075e-SJC"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="93188be17fb9075e-SJC">

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            timeout: 5000,

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
            },
            retrieveEntity: function (ms) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                if (ms == undefined || ms === '') {
                    ms = this.timeout;
                }

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res.data);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('failed to retrieve entity from local storage: ' + err);
                        });
                    // Set up the timeout
                    setTimeout(function () {
                        reject('Promise timed out ' + ms + ' ms');
                    }, ms);
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage due to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {
                            doi: doi,
                            entityid: entityId,
                            entityTitle: entityTitle,
                            eventGroupKey: 'b9a8edfc-9ba6-4e28-94f1-193b11af4fb1'
                        }

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    }).fail(function (status) {
                        return reject(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (i = 0; i < allSsoInstitutions.length; i++) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        if(allSsoInstitutions.length === 0 && true){
                            self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, null, null)
                                .then(function () {
                                    console.log('No Entity found');
                                }, function (err) {
                                    console.log('failed to get the none entity status' ,err);
                                });
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            }).catch(function (err) {
                                reject(err);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();

                    if ($('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').length > 0) {
                        let institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox = $('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').get(0);
                        if (!$(institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox).is(":checked")) {
                            return;
                        }
                    }

                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

src="https://www2.snapengage.com/chatjs/ServiceGetConfig?w=921a4ec7-cecf-43a6-afa5-6cd1346520b1"></script><script charset="utf-8" src="https://pubs.acs.org/products/achs/releasedAssets/js/lazy-imports-6922fe6a4ca6b2e0cd9a.js"></script><script type="text/javascript" src="/specs/products/achs/releasedAssets/public/mathjax-0a9852ad89643b94fe5099b753f6a294/MathJax.js?config=TeX-AMS-MML_HTMLorMML"></script><script type="text/x-mathjax-config;executed=true">MathJax.Hub.Config({
            menuSettings: {
                zoom: "Click",
                zscale: "150%"
            },
            SVG: {
                fonts: ["STIX-Web"],
                linebreaks: { automatic: true },
            },
            "HTML-CSS": {
                fonts: ["STIX"],
                linebreaks: { automatic: true },
                scale: 90,
            },
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("mml Jax Ready", function () {
            var MML = MathJax.ElementJax.mml;
            MML.mi.prototype.setTeXclass = function (prev) {
                this.getPrevClass(prev);
                return this;
            };
            MML.mfrac.Augment({
                setTeXclass: function (prev) {
                    this.getPrevClass(prev);
                    for (var i = 0, m = this.data.length; i < m; i++) {
                        if (this.data[i]) this.data[i].setTeXclass();
                    }
                    return this;
                }
            });
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("SVG Jax Ready", function () {
            var FONT = MathJax.OutputJax.SVG.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-Web-variant"] || MathJax.OutputJax.SVG.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-variant"];
            delete MathJax.ElementJax.mml.mo.prototype.remapChars['°'];
            if (FONT) {
                FONT.remap[0xB0]= [0x25E6, "normal"];
                FONT.remap[0x2A]= [0x2217, "normal"];
            }

        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("MathML Jax Ready", function () {
            var PARSE = MathJax.InputJax.MathML.Parse;
            var ADD = PARSE.prototype.AddChildren;
            PARSE.Augment({
                AddChildren: function (mml, node) {
                    ADD.call(this, mml, node);
                    if (mml.type === 'mrow') {
                        var first = mml.data[0], last = mml.data[mml.data.length-1];
                        if (mml.open && !mml.data[0].Get('stretchy')) delete mml.open;
                        if (mml.close && !mml.data[mml.data.length - 1].Get('stretchy')) delete mml.close;
                    }
                }
            });
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("HTML-CSS Jax Ready", function () {
            var HTMLCSS = MathJax.OutputJax['HTML-CSS'];
            var DELIMITERS = HTMLCSS.FONTDATA.DELIMITERS;
            var FONT = HTMLCSS.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-variant"] || HTMLCSS.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-Web-variant"]

            var MML = MathJax.ElementJax.mml;

            MML.mrow.Augment({
              _HTMLlineBreaks: MML.mrow.prototype.HTMLlineBreaks,
              HTMLlineBreaks: function (span) {

                if (this.parent.linebreakContainer && this.Get("display") === "inline") return false;
                return this._HTMLlineBreaks(span);
              }
            });


            DELIMITERS[0x0305] = {dir: "H", alias: 0x00AF};
            DELIMITERS[0x033F] = {dir: "H", alias: 0x003D};
            DELIMITERS[0x20E1] = {dir: "H", alias: 0x2194};

            if (FONT) {
                FONT.remap[0xB0]= [0x25E6, "normal"];
                FONT.remap[0x2A]= [0x2217, "normal"];
            }

            delete MathJax.ElementJax.mml.mo.prototype.remapChars['°'];
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("HTML-CSS multiline Ready", function () {
            var HTMLCSS = MathJax.OutputJax["HTML-CSS"];
            var MML = MathJax.ElementJax.mml;
            var PENALTY = MML.mbase.prototype.HTMLlinebreakPenalty;

            MML.msqrt.Augment({
                linebreakContainer: false,
                HTMLbetterBreak: function () {return false}
            });
            MML.mroot.Augment({
                linebreakContainer: false,
                HTMLbetterBreak: function () {return false}
            });
            MML.mfrac.Augment({
                linebreakContainer: false,
                HTMLbetterBreak: function () {return false}
            });
            MML.mspace.Augment({
                defaultDef: {
                    indentalign: MML.INDENTALIGN.AUTO,
                    indentshift: "0",
                    indenttarget: "",
                    indentalignfirst: MML.INDENTALIGN.INDENTALIGN,
                    indentshiftfirst: MML.INDENTSHIFT.INDENTSHIFT,
                    indentalignlast: MML.INDENTALIGN.INDENTALIGN,
                    indentshiftlast: MML.INDENTSHIFT.INDENTSHIFT
                },
                HTMLbetterBreak: function (info,state) {
                    if (info.values && info.values.id === this.spanID) {return false}
                    var values = this.getValues(
                        "linebreak",
                        "indentalign","indentshift",
                        "indentalignfirst","indentshiftfirst",
                        "indentalignlast","indentshiftlast"
                    );
                    var linebreakValue = values.linebreak;
                    if (!linebreakValue || this.hasDimAttr()) {
                        linebreakValue = MML.LINEBREAK.AUTO;
                    }
                    var W = info.scanW, span = this.HTMLspanElement(), w = span.bbox.w;
                    if (span.style.paddingLeft) {w += HTMLCSS.unEm(span.style.paddingLeft)}
                    if (W - info.shift === 0) {return false} // don't break at zero width
                    var offset = HTMLCSS.linebreakWidth - W;

                    if (state.n === 0 && (values.indentshiftfirst !== state.VALUES.indentshiftfirst ||
                        values.indentalignfirst !== state.VALUES.indentalignfirst)) {
                        var align = this.HTMLgetAlign(state,values),
                            shift = this.HTMLgetShift(state,values,align);
                        offset += (info.shift - shift);
                    }

                    var penalty = Math.floor(offset / HTMLCSS.linebreakWidth * 1000);
                    if (penalty < 0) {penalty = PENALTY.toobig - 3*penalty}
                    penalty += info.nest * PENALTY.nestfactor;

                    var linebreak = PENALTY[linebreakValue]||0;
                    if (linebreakValue === MML.LINEBREAK.AUTO && w >= PENALTY.spacelimit &&
                        !this.mathbackground && !this.background)
                    {linebreak = [(w+PENALTY.spaceoffset)*PENALTY.spacefactor]}
                    if (!MathJax.Object.isArray(linebreak)) {
                        if (linebreak || offset >= 0) {penalty = linebreak * info.nest}
                    } else {penalty = Math.max(1,penalty + linebreak[0] * info.nest)}

                    if (penalty >= info.penalty) {return false}
                    info.penalty = penalty; info.values = values; info.W = W; info.w = w;
                    values.lineleading = state.VALUES.lineleading;
                    values.linebreakstyle = "before"; values.id = this.spanID;
                    return true;
                }
            });


            
            PENALTY.goodbreak = [-400];

        });</script><style type="text/css">.MathJax_Hover_Frame {border-radius: .25em; -webkit-border-radius: .25em; -moz-border-radius: .25em; -khtml-border-radius: .25em; box-shadow: 0px 0px 15px #83A; -webkit-box-shadow: 0px 0px 15px #83A; -moz-box-shadow: 0px 0px 15px #83A; -khtml-box-shadow: 0px 0px 15px #83A; border: 1px solid #A6D ! important; display: inline-block; position: absolute}

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="93188be17fb9075e-SJC">
var dfpReady = false;
$(document).ready(function() {
    // var journalTitle = 'nano';
    var taxonomyKeywords = $('.article_header-taxonomy');
    var articleKeyword = $('meta[name="keywords"]');
    var articleTitle = $('meta[name="dc.Title"]');
    var articleDescription = $('meta[name="dc.Description"]');
    var abstractKeyword = $('p.articleBody_abstractText:contains("Keywords: ")');
    var searchTerms = [];

    if (taxonomyKeywords.length > 0) {
        $(taxonomyKeywords).children(".rlist--inline").children("li").each(function() {
            searchTerms.push($(this).text());
        });
    }
    else if (articleKeyword.length > 0) { 
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleKeyword.prop('content').split(', '));
    }
    else if (abstractKeyword.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(abstractKeyword.text().split("Keywords: ")[1].split('; '));
    }
    else if (articleDescription.length > 0) {
        $(articleDescription).each(function() {
            articleDescriptionKeywords = $(this).prop('content');
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/.,/g,"");
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/\s{2,}/g," ");
            searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleDescriptionKeywords.split(' '));
        });
    }

    if (articleTitle.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleTitle.prop('content').split(' '));
    }

    googletag.cmd.push(function() {
        var mappingLeader = googletag.sizeMapping().
        addSize([750, 200], [728, 90]). 
        addSize([0, 0], [320, 50]).
        build();
        //leaderboard
        googletag.defineSlot('/8868/journal/nano/article', [728, 90], 'dfp-journal-article-leaderboard').defineSizeMapping(mappingLeader).setTargeting('location', 'leaderboard1').setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //recommend
        googletag.defineSlot("/8868/journal/nano/article", [1, 1], "dfp-journal-article-recommend").setTargeting("ntvPlacement", ["1100167"]).setTargeting("location", "recommend").setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //googletag.pubads().enableSingleRequest();
        googletag.pubads().collapseEmptyDivs();
        googletag.pubads().setTargeting('inst',dartInstitutionType).setTargeting('memb',dartMember);
        googletag.pubads().addEventListener("slotRenderEnded", function(event) {
            console.log(event.slot.getSlotElementId() + " isEmpty: " + event.isEmpty + " | creative id: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            if((event.isEmpty === false) && (event.slot.getSlotElementId() != "dfp-journal-article-recommend")) {
                $("#" + event.slot.getSlotElementId()).parents(".advertisement").slideDown();
                console.log("ad display: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            }
            // else {
            //     console.log("no ad found");
            // }
        });
        googletag.enableServices();
        dfpReady = true;
    });
});
</script>

class="figure-viewer_image"><a href="#" title="Next" class="figure-viewer_next icon-angle-right" style="display: inline;"></a><a href="#" title="Previous" class="figure-viewer_prev icon-angle-left" style="display: inline;"></a><div class="figure-viewer_image-content"><img src="" alt="Figure 1" class="fv-img"><img title="Download Hi-Res Image" target="_blank" class="figure-viewer_hi-res-link"><i class="icon-file-image-o"></i><span>Download Hi-Res Image</span></a><span class="fv-separator"></span><a href="#" title="Download to MS-PowerPoint" class="figure-viewer_ms-p-link"><i class="icon-file-powerpoint-o"></i><span>Download to MS-PowerPoint</span></a><span class="cit-this-container"><a href="/action/showCitFormats?doi=10.1021/acsnano.1c03056&amp;href=/doi/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056" title="Cite This" class="figure-viewer-cite-this-link"><i class="icon-check-circle"></i><span><strong>Cite This:</strong></span></a><span class="article_header-cite-this figure-viewer-cite-this"><span class="cit-fg-title"><i>ACS Nano</i></span><span class="cit-fg-year"> 2021</span><span class="cit-fg-volume">, 15</span><span class="cit-fg-issue">, 8</span><span class="cit-fg-pageRange">, 13307-13318</span></span></span></div></div></div></div></div><input type="hidden" name="ancac3" id="copyRights" value="/pb-assets/json/journal-info-1744387780883.json"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone5" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone5"><!-- Article Refresh Event Tracking -->
<script nonce="93188be17fb9075e-SJC">
$(function() {
    var serialCode = "ancac3";
    var books = ["reagents", "symposium", "advances", "medichemreviews", "styleguide"]
    if(books.includes(serialCode) === false) {
        // default click action
        $("[data-id]").on("mousedown", function(e) {
            var currentClickID = $(this).attr("data-id");

            if(currentClickID.includes("_hover") === false) {
                if(currentClickID.match("^article_") && !currentClickID.match("^article_abstract_CC")) {   
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Bilateral Interfaces in In&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;Se&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt;-CoIn&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;-CoSe&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Heterostructures for High-Rate Reversible Sodium Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsnano.1c03056", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                }
            }
        });
        
        // Access Management icons hover
        var articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        var articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent === false) {
                articleAccessManagementIconHover = true;
                var articleAccessManagementHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleAccessManagementIconHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Bilateral Interfaces in In&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;Se&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt;-CoIn&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;-CoSe&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Heterostructures for High-Rate Reversible Sodium Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsnano.1c03056", "Article_Element": articleAccessManagementHover });
    
                        articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        });
    
        // articleRightsPermissionsLink hover
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent === false) {
                articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = true;
                var articleRightsHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Bilateral Interfaces in In&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;Se&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt;-CoIn&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;-CoSe&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Heterostructures for High-Rate Reversible Sodium Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsnano.1c03056", "Article_Element": articleRightsHover });
    
                        articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        });
    
        // Author hover
        var articleAuthorHover = false
        var articleAuthorHoverEvent = false
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if((articleAuthorHoverEvent === false) && ($(this).parent().hasClass("view-affs") === false)) {
                articleAuthorHover = true;
                var authorInfoHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAuthorHover === true) && (articleAuthorHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Bilateral Interfaces in In&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;Se&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt;-CoIn&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;-CoSe&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Heterostructures for High-Rate Reversible Sodium Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsnano.1c03056", "Article_Element": authorInfoHover });
    
                        articleAuthorHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAuthorHover = false;
        });
    
        // CC License hover
        var articleAbstractCCHover = false
        var articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = false
        var articleDrawerCCHover = false
        var articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = false
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if($(this).attr("data-id")) {
                if(($(this).attr("data-id") === "article_drawer_CC-License") && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleDrawerCCHover = true;
                    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleDrawerCCHover === true) && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Bilateral Interfaces in In&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;Se&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt;-CoIn&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;-CoSe&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Heterostructures for High-Rate Reversible Sodium Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsnano.1c03056", "Article_Element": "article_drawer_CC-License_hover" });
    
                            articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
                else if(($(this).attr("data-id").match("^article_abstract_CC")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleAbstractCCHover = true;
    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Bilateral Interfaces in In&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;Se&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt;-CoIn&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;-CoSe&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Heterostructures for High-Rate Reversible Sodium Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsnano.1c03056", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                            articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
            }
            else if(($(this).hasClass("article__cc-license__link")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = true;
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Bilateral Interfaces in In&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;Se&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt;-CoIn&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;-CoSe&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Heterostructures for High-Rate Reversible Sodium Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsnano.1c03056", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                        articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            if(articleAbstractCCHover === true) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = false;
            }
            if(articleDrawerCCHover = true) {
                articleDrawerCCHover = false;
            }
        });
        
        // show recommeneded click delay
        var intervalCount = 0;
        var showRecommendedInterval = setInterval(function() {
            intervalCount += 100;
            if($(".show-recommended__wrapper .show-recommended").length > 0) {
                clearInterval(showRecommendedInterval);
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowMore']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Bilateral Interfaces in In&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;Se&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt;-CoIn&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;-CoSe&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Heterostructures for High-Rate Reversible Sodium Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsnano.1c03056", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowLess']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Bilateral Interfaces in In&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;Se&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt;-CoIn&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;-CoSe&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Heterostructures for High-Rate Reversible Sodium Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsnano.1c03056", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
            }
        }, 100);
    }
});
</script>

Xiao</a></span></div></div></div></span></li><li><span><span class="hlFld-ContribAuthor" tabindex="0" data-id="article_author_info" property="author">Xinyan Li</span><div class="loa-info class="articleMetrics_count"><h2>Citations</h2><div class="articleMetrics-val"><a href="#citeThis" class="internalNav">143</a></div></div></div></div><div class="articleMetrics_about"><div class="base data-db-target-of="aboutArticleMetrics" id="about-article-metrics" class="dropBlock__holder"><button class="articleMetrics_close"> <i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-close_thin"></i><span Find more information on<a href="https://help.altmetric.com/support/solutions/articles/6000233311-how-is-the-altmetric-attention-score-calculated"> the Altmetric Attention Score and how the score is calculated.</a></p></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="article_abstract"><div class="article_abstract-title" id="Abstract" tabindex="0"><h2>Abstract</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div><div class="article_abstract-content hlFld-Abstract" id="abstractBox" property="description"><figure id="_i1" data-index="0" class="article__inlineFigure article_abstract-img"><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img class="inline-fig internalNav" src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056/asset/images/medium/nn1c03056_0006.gif" alt="" id="tgr1" property="image" style="width:405px; height:275px"></button><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056/asset/images/large/nn1c03056_0006.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsnano.1c03056&amp;id=_i1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p class="articleBody_abstractText">Metal selenides are considered as a group of promising candidates as the anode material for sodium-ion batteries due to their high theoretical capacity. However, the intrinsically low electrical and ionic conductivities as well as huge volume change during the charge-discharge process give rise to an inferior sodium storage capability, which severely hinders their practical application. Herein, we fabricated In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub> hollow nanorods composed of In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoIn<sub>2</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub> by growing cobalt-based zeolitic imidazolate framework ZIF-67 on the surface of indium-based metal–organic framework MIL-68, followed by <i>in situ</i> gaseous selenization. Because of the CoIn<sub>2</sub> alloy phase in between In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub> and CoSe<sub>2</sub>, a heterostructure consisting of two alloy/selenide interfaces has been successfully constructed, offering synergistically enhanced electrical conductivity, Na diffusion process, and structural stability, in comparison to the single CoIn<sub>2</sub>-free interface with only two metal selenides. As expected, this nanoconstruction delivers a high reversible capacity of 297.5 and 205.5 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 5 and 10 A g<sup>–1</sup> after 2000 cycles, respectively, and a superior rate performance of 371.6 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at even 20 A g<sup>–1</sup>.</p></div><div class="article__cc-license"><div class="article__cc-license__body"><p class="article__cc-license__para">This publication is licensed under the terms of your
                            institutional subscription.
                            <a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D13307%26pageCount%3D12%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DShuhao%2BXiao%252C%2BXinyan%2BLi%252C%2BWensi%2BZhang%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D15%26issueNum%3D8%26contentID%3Dacsnano.1c03056%26title%3DBilateral%2BInterfaces%2Bin%2BIn2Se3-CoIn2-CoSe2%2BHeterostructures%2Bfor%2BHigh-Rate%2BReversible%2BSodium%2BStorage%26numPages%3D12%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1936-0851%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Dancac3%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D13318%26publicationDate%3DAugust%2B2021" class="link--bold">Request reuse permissions.</a></p></div></div><span class="hidden" property="publisher">ACS Publications</span><div class="article_header-article-copyright">Copyright © 2021 American Chemical Society</div><div class="article_header-footer-right"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone7" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone7"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div><div class="article__tags article__tags--subjects"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Subjects</h3><div tabindex="0" class="article__tags__tooltip"><div aria-describedby="tooltip-subjects" class="article__tags__icon"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are subjects</span></div><p id="tooltip-subjects" role="tooltip" class="article__tags__diff">
                                        Article subjects are automatically applied from the ACS Subject Taxonomy and describe the scientific concepts and themes of the article.</p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=290830&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Diffusion"> Diffusion </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291323&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Heterostructures"> Heterostructures </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=290817&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Interfaces"> Interfaces </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=290797&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Metals"> Metals </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291607&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Selenides"> Selenides </a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article__tags article__tags--keywords hlFld-Abstract"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Keywords</h3><div class="article__tags__tooltip" tabindex="0"><div class="article__tags__icon" aria-describedby="tooltip-keywords"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are keywords</span></div><p class="article__tags__diff" id="tooltip-keywords" role="tooltip">
                        Article keywords are supplied by the authors and highlight key terms and topics
                        of the paper.
                    </p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Metal+Selenide&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_metal%20selenide">metal selenide</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Heterostructure&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_heterostructure">heterostructure</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Multi-interface&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_multi-interface">multi-interface</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Anode+Material&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_anode%20material">anode material</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Sodium-ion+Battery&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_sodium-ion%20battery">sodium-ion battery</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article_content"><div class="article_content-table hlFld-FullText"><div class="article_content-row"><div class="article_content-left" property="articleBody" style="width: 384px;"><div id="sec1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="NLM_p first">With the fast development of portable electronic devices and electric vehicles, the demand for rechargeable batteries with high energy/power densities and long cycle life is growing tremendously over the years. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1 ref2" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref1 ref2" aria-label="reference 1 and 2">(1,2)</a> Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), which have a similar energy storage mechanism to lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), are considered as a suitable replacement to LIBs due to the merits of rich natural resources, low cost, and appropriate redox potential (−2.71 <i>vs</i> SHE) of Na. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref3" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref3" aria-label="reference 3">(3)</a> However, the radius of Na atoms (∼1.09 Å) is 55% larger than that of Li, which would cause sluggish diffusion kinetics and large volume change during the electrochemical processes, resulting in an inferior sodium storage capability, thus limiting the practical application of SIBs. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref4" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref4" aria-label="reference 4">(4)</a> It is thus an urgent need to explore active materials to overcome the above-mentioned shortcomings.</div><div class="NLM_p">In the past decade, various anode materials have been extensively investigated for SIBs, such as carbonaceous materials, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref5 ref6" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref5 ref6" aria-label="reference 5 and 6">(5,6)</a> alloys, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref7 ref8" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref7 ref8" aria-label="reference 7 and 8">(7,8)</a> metal oxides, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref9 ref10" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref9 ref10" aria-label="reference 9 and 10">(9,10)</a> and dichalcogenides. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref11 ref12" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref11 ref12" aria-label="reference 11 and 12">(11,12)</a> As a promising anode material for SIBs, metal selenides have received much attention considering their high theoretical capacity and volumetric capacity density. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref13 ref14" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref13 ref14" aria-label="reference 13 and 14">(13,14)</a> In addition, owing to the large atom radius of selenium, the metal–selenium bonds are weaker than the metal–oxygen and metal–sulfur counterparts, leading to an improved efficiency of the conversion reaction in the selenides. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref15" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref15" aria-label="reference 15">(15)</a> Take cobalt selenide (CoSe<sub>2</sub>) as an example, it has stable chemical properties and environmental friendliness; thus it has been reported as a promising anode material and extensively studied in SIBs. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref16 ref17 ref18" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref16 ref17 ref18" aria-label="reference 16 to 18">(16−18)</a> However, like many other selenides, it still suffers from several drawbacks such as low intrinsic electronic conductivity, sluggish Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics, and huge volume variation during Na<sup>+</sup> intercalation/extraction processes, leading to inferior rate performance and poor cycling stability. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref19 ref20" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref19 ref20" aria-label="reference 19 and 20">(19,20)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">In order to boost the sodium storage abilities of metal selenides, many efforts have been devoted, such as composition hybridization, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref21" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref21" aria-label="reference 21">(21)</a> electrolyte modification, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref22" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref22" aria-label="reference 22">(22)</a> and nanostructure engineering. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref14 ref23 ref24" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref14 ref23 ref24" aria-label="reference 14, 23 and 24">(14,23,24)</a> Recently, constructing heterostructures has shown to be an efficient strategy owing to the synergistic effect between the different components at the interface. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref25 ref26 ref27" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref25 ref26 ref27" aria-label="reference 25 to 27">(25−27)</a> According to the previous studies, an internal electric field will be established in the heterostructure through a spontaneous electron migration across the interface. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref28" aria-label="reference 28">(28)</a> This offers an extra driving force to accelerate the charge transfer, resulting in greatly enhanced electrical and ionic conductivities, thus giving rise to superior rate capability and cycle life of the electrode materials. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref29" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref29" aria-label="reference 29">(29)</a> In addition, the active materials with heterostructures are often imbued with an improved structural stability compared to the phase-pure counterparts. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref30" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref30" aria-label="reference 30">(30)</a> Because of these distinct advantages, constructing heterotructures with two different metal selenides has been employed to boost the electrochemical performance for SIBs. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref31 ref32" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref31 ref32" aria-label="reference 31 and 32">(31,32)</a> For instance, the SnSe<sub>2</sub>/ZnSe heterostructure delivered an improved electrochemical performance at high current densities due to its faster Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion rate than that of SnSe<sub>2</sub> and ZnSe. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref21" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref21" aria-label="reference 21">(21)</a> Because of the beneficial effect of these heterostructures, it is thus highly desirable to construct more interfaces in the active materials to better discover the potential of this category of composite materials. However, it is practically challenging to introduce multiple heterointerfaces considering the compatibility of different components and the complexity of the synthesis approaches achieving such composites.</div><div class="NLM_p last">In order to address these issues, herein, we fabricated metal–organic framework (MOF)-derived hollow nanorods consisting of heterostructured In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>-CoIn<sub>2</sub>-CoSe<sub>2</sub> with two different interfaces. A rodlike indium-based MOF, MIL-68, was first synthesized as a template for the subsequent coating of a cobalt-based MOF, ZIF-67, giving rise to a MIL-68@ZIF-67 core–shell structure. Such a composite was then selenized under inert gas, transforming the metal components into the corresponding selenides, accompanied by an inside-out hollowing process. By tuning the selenization temperature, the CoIn<sub>2</sub> alloy phase could be formed in addition to the metal selenides, giving rise to a heterostructure with In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>-CoIn<sub>2</sub> and CoSe<sub>2</sub>-CoIn<sub>2</sub> bilateral interfaces. The theoretical calculation results revealed that such a heterostructure not only enhanced the adsorption and reduced the diffusion barrier of Na atoms but also promoted spontaneous electron transfer across these interfaces, resulting in the improved electrical conductivity, Na ions diffusion process, and structural stability of the as-prepared hollow nanorods. As expected, this tri-phase composite delivered a high reversible capacity of 297.5 and 205.5 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 5 and 10 A g<sup>–1</sup> after 2000 cycles, respectively, and a superior rate performance of 371.6 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at even 20 A g<sup>–1</sup>.</div></div><div id="sec2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i2">Results/Discussion</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">The overall fabrication procedure of the composite hollow nanorods is illustrated in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>a. As both the starting template and indium source, MIL-68 (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>b) with a hexagonal prism structure was first prepared. ZIF-67 was then uniformly deposited on the surface of MIL-68 at room temperature (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>c). It is interesting to observe that, instead of the usual rhombic dodecahedral structure, the coated ZIF-67 showed as nanoparticles without a well-defined morphology, forming a densely packed outer layer which exhibited a corn-like morphology. This could be probably attributed to the high affinity between these two MOFs, giving rise to a fast, yet uniform, nucleation of ZIF-67 on MIL-68. The different weight ratios, <i>i.e.</i>, 1:8, 1:6, 1:4, and 1:3, between cobalt nitrate and MIL-68 during the coating process have been investigated, and the SEM image of the corresponding sample is shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056/suppl_file/nn1c03056_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S1</a>. When the content of cobalt nitrate was at a relatively high level, the resulting ZIF-67 showed an irregular shape with a large particle size. As the concentration of cobalt nitrate in the solution decreased, the ZIF-67 nanoparticles got significantly smaller and managed to uniformly deposit on the surface of MIL-68. After carbonization, the particles on the surface of the hexagonal prism condensed into nanoflakes (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>d). Finally, the hollow nanorods were obtained <i>via</i> a gas-phase selenization under the flow of Ar/H<sub>2</sub>, while the hexagonal prism nanostructure could be largely retained (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>e). As expected, In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-400 demonstrated an almost identical morphology as In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450 (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056/suppl_file/nn1c03056_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S2</a>), whereas In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub> exhibited severe structural collapse, which could be probably due to the absence of the outer ZIF-67 protective layer. Phase-pure CoSe<sub>2</sub> demonstrated aggregations of well-faceted particles, resembling the morphology of the parental ZIF-67.</div><figure id="fig1" data-index="1" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 1</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056/asset/images/medium/nn1c03056_0001.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056/asset/images/large/nn1c03056_0001.jpeg" id="gr1" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 1. (a) Schematic illustration of the synthetic process. SEM images of (b) In-MOF, (c) In-MOF@ZIF-67, (d) In<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@CoO<sub><i>x</i></sub>, and (e) In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450; (f) TEM image, (g) HRTEM image, and (h) HAADF-STEM image and corresponding elemental mapping of In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056/asset/images/large/nn1c03056_0001.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsnano.1c03056&amp;id=fig1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">The internal structure of as-prepared In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450 is elucidated by transmission electron microscopy (TEM), and a well-defined inner cavity can be clearly observed (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>f). The generation of the hollow structure could possibly be attributed to the Kirkendall effect, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref33" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref33" aria-label="reference 33">(33)</a> which has been reported in other types of MOF-derived hollow materials. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref34" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref34" aria-label="reference 34">(34)</a> Specifically, during the selenization process which initiated at the surface of the MOFs, selenium atoms diffused from the surface to the interior of the nanorods while indium atoms flow outward at a different rate. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref35" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref35" aria-label="reference 35">(35)</a> Finally, the discrepant diffusion rates of the two kinds of atoms would be balanced by the movement of voids, thus giving rise to the hollow interior and a thin shell with a thickness of less than 100 nm. As displayed in the high-resolution TEM (HRTEM) result of In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450 (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>g), three different sets of lattice fringes are clearly visible. The interplanar spacings of 0.52 and 0.26 nm were identified, corresponding to the (102) plane of hexagonal In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub> (JCPDS: 71-0250) and the (111) plane of orthorhombic CoSe<sub>2</sub> (JCPDS: 53-0449), respectively. At the same time, the third lattice fringes with a spacing of 0.27 nm correspond to the (311) plane of orthorhombic CoIn<sub>2</sub> (JCPDS: 71-0329). These three different phases contributed to a heterostructure with two interfaces which were marked by dashed lines with different colors. Even though In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-400 (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056/suppl_file/nn1c03056_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S3</a>) exhibited the same hollow structure as In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450, only two selenide phases were observed under HRTEM, corresponding to a single interface of In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>-CoSe<sub>2</sub>. Meanwhile, the uniform distributions of C, In, Co, and Se elements of an individual In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450 hollow nanorod were confirmed by element mapping (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>h), suggesting the formation of a homogeneous solid solution of In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>, CoSe<sub>2</sub>, and CoIn<sub>2</sub>.</div><div class="NLM_p">Such a three-phase composition was further verified by X-ray diffraction (XRD). As depicted in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056/suppl_file/nn1c03056_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S4</a>, such a selenization method was proven to be quite effective in that all the precursor samples were completely converted into the corresponding selenides even at a relatively low temperature of 400 °C, with no identifiable parental or impurity phases. Moreover, when the temperature was increased to 450 °C, most of the identified peaks of In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450 could be attributed to hexagonal In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub> (JCPDS: 71-0250) and orthorhombic CoSe<sub>2</sub> (JCPDS: 53-0449). Additional sharp peaks which are located at 31.7° and 33.6° could be ascribed to orthorhombic CoIn<sub>2</sub> (JCPDS: 71-0329). According to the Co-In phase diagram, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref36" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref36" aria-label="reference 36">(36)</a> the formation of the binary alloys between Co and In is quite sensitive to the molar ratio and annealing temperature. Theoretically, the Co/(Co + In) ratio in CoIn<sub>2</sub> is about 0.33, and from the phase diagram, at this composition, the lowest formation temperature of this binary alloy is 700 K, which is 427 °C. As a result, the CoIn<sub>2</sub> alloy only formed in In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450 whose annealing temperature is 450 °C. Only metal selenides were found in In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-400, as the heating process was carried out at 400 °C. Additionally, the peak at around 52° in the XRD pattern was labeled as cubic CoSe<sub>2</sub>, which has been commonly observed in the gas-phase selenization process and reported in previous work. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref19" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref19" aria-label="reference 19">(19)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">Quantitative analysis by inductively coupled plasma atomic emission spectrometry (ICP-AES) suggested that the atomic ratio of In and Co in In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450 and In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-400 was 1:0.56 and 1:0.68, respectively. Subsequently, the weight content of carbon in this sample was measured <i>via</i> thermogravimetric (TG) analysis in air (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056/suppl_file/nn1c03056_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S4d</a>). The main weight loss from 340 to 550 °C can be ascribed to the volatilization of SeO<sub>2</sub> and the combustion of carbon. After that, the final residue with a mass content of 42.9 and 38.7 wt % at 800 °C for In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450 and In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-400, respectively, could be attributed to the oxide phases of In<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> and Co<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub>. In tandem with the ICP-AES results, the mass content of In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub> and CoSe<sub>2</sub> could be calculated to be 62.7 and 28.2 wt % in In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450, respectively, and 54.6% and 29.6% in In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-400. Therefore, the weight percentage of carbon in the composites of In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450 and In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-400 was computed to be 9.1% and 15.8%, respectively. The surface structures of In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450 and In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-400 were further analyzed by the Brunauer–Emmett–Teller (BET) method. The N<sub>2</sub> adsorption and desorption isotherms of the as-prepared samples (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056/suppl_file/nn1c03056_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S5</a>) belong to a typical IV adsorption isotherm with a type H3 hysteresis loop, suggesting the combination of meso- and micropores in the hollow nanorods. Moreover, In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450 possesses a specific surface area and a total pore volume of 88.3 m<sup>2</sup> g<sup>–1</sup> and 0.066 cm<sup>3</sup> g<sup>–1</sup>, respectively, which are higher than those of In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-400 (48.6 m<sup>2</sup> g<sup>–1</sup> and 0.051 cm<sup>3</sup> g<sup>–1</sup>). As shown in the inset in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056/suppl_file/nn1c03056_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S5</a>, In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450 and In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-400 exhibited pore size distributions generally in the range of 2–25 nm, and average pore sizes at about 1.5 and 2.1 nm, respectively. To investigate the graphitization degree of the carbon in In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450, In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-400, In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>, and CoSe<sub>2</sub>, Raman spectroscopy was carried out at the wavenumber of 900–2100 cm<sup>–1</sup>. As shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056/suppl_file/nn1c03056_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S6</a>, the four samples all display two strong peaks located at 1330 and 1587 cm<sup>–1</sup>, corresponding to the D band and the G band, respectively. The In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450 exhibits an intensity ratio (<i>I</i><sub>D</sub>/<i>I</i><sub>G</sub>) of 0.93, which is higher than that of the other three samples, indicating a lower graphitization level.</div><div class="NLM_p">In addition, the valence and chemical states of In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450 and In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-400 were determined by X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS). In the Co 2p spectrum of In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450 (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>b), the strong peaks located at 796.9 and 780.7 eV can be ascribed to Co 2p<sub>3/2</sub> and 2p<sub>1/2</sub> of the Co<sup>2+</sup> state, respectively, which belong to the CoSe<sub>2</sub> phase. Meanwhile, the peaks centered at 793.4 and 778.3 eV are characteristics of the Co<sup>3+</sup> state. The existence of Co<sup>3+</sup> could be attributed to the partial oxidation on the CoSe<sub>2</sub> surface in air. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref18" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref18" aria-label="reference 18">(18)</a> Noticeably, compared to In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450, In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-400 has a higher intensity of the Co<sup>3+</sup> peak, which could be due to the lower calcination temperature of 400 °C. This led to the formation of less stable CoSe<sub>2</sub> that was easier to be oxidized during the XPS test. In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450 was selenized under a higher temperature of 450 °C and possessed the CoIn<sub>2</sub> alloy. With both Co<sup>2+</sup> and Co<sup>0</sup>, the oxidation to Co<sup>3+</sup> could thus be more difficult, resulting in a lower peak intensity of Co<sup>3+</sup>. Moreover, the In 3d spectrum (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>c) can be deconvoluted into two peaks at 445.0 and 452.5 eV, corresponding to In 3d<sub>5/2</sub> and 3d<sub>3/2</sub>, respectively. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref37" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref37" aria-label="reference 37">(37)</a> Notably, compared to In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-400, the peaks in the Co 2p and In 3d spectra of In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450 shifted to higher binding energies, revealing an enhanced electronic coupling between the elements, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref21" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref21" aria-label="reference 21">(21)</a> which could be due to the formed CoIn<sub>2</sub> alloy phase. Furthermore, as shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>d, the Se 3d spectrum clearly exhibited two peaks which were located at 54.2 and 55.4 eV, corresponding to Se 3d<sub>5/2</sub> and 3d<sub>3/2</sub>, respectively. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref38" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref38" aria-label="reference 38">(38)</a> The additional peaks centered at 58.6 and 59.2 eV could be assigned to the Co 3p<sub>3/2</sub> and 3p<sub>1/2</sub>, respectively, which is consistent with a previous report about CoSe<sub>2</sub>. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref19" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref19" aria-label="reference 19">(19)</a></div><figure id="fig2" data-index="2" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 2</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056/asset/images/medium/nn1c03056_0002.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056/asset/images/large/nn1c03056_0002.jpeg" id="gr2" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 2. (a) XRD pattern of In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450. High-resolution XPS spectra of (b) Co 2p, (c) In 3d, and (d) Se 3d of various samples: (I) In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450 and (II) In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-400.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056/asset/images/large/nn1c03056_0002.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsnano.1c03056&amp;id=fig2"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">The electrochemical performances of In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450, In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-400, pure In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>, and CoSe<sub>2</sub> were investigated in a coin-type 2032 cell utilizing sodium metal as the counter electrode. The cyclic voltammetry (CV) of these four samples was measured to explore the various electrochemical reactions with a voltage window of 0.01–2.5 V at 0.1 mV s<sup>–1</sup> (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>a and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056/suppl_file/nn1c03056_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S7</a>). Noticeably, the peaks in the CVs of In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450 and In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-400 are comparable, indicating that the presence of CoIn<sub>2</sub> would not interfere with the Na<sup>+</sup> storage behavior of other active components. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref39 ref40" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref39 ref40" aria-label="reference 39 and 40">(39,40)</a> As discussed in previous works, the main reactions of Na<sup>+</sup> storage in CoSe<sub>2</sub> during the discharge-charge cycles are as follows: <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref41" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref41" aria-label="reference 41">(41)</a></div><figure id="fig3" data-index="3" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 3</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056/asset/images/medium/nn1c03056_0003.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056/asset/images/large/nn1c03056_0003.jpeg" id="gr3" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 3. Electrochemical performance of SIB. (a) CV profiles of In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450 at a scan rate of 0.1 mV s<sup>–1</sup>. (b) Discharge/charge curves of In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450 at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>. (c) Cycling performance at 0.5 A g<sup>–1</sup> and (d) rate capability of (I) In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450, (II) In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-400, (III) In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>, and (IV) CoSe<sub>2</sub>. (e) Long-term cyclability of the In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450 anode. (f) Comparison of rate performances between In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450 and other selenide-based SIB anodes. (g) Discharge/charge curves and (h) cycling performance of a In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450//Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> full cell at 0.5 A g<sup>–1</sup>.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056/asset/images/large/nn1c03056_0003.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsnano.1c03056&amp;id=fig3"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">Discharge:<span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq1"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056/asset/images/medium/nn1c03056_m001.gif" alt="" id="_i3"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(1)</span></div></div></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq2"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056/asset/images/medium/nn1c03056_m002.gif" alt="" id="_i4"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(2)</span></div></div></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq3"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056/asset/images/medium/nn1c03056_m003.gif" alt="" id="_i5"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(3)</span></div></div></span></div><div class="NLM_p">Charged:<span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq4"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056/asset/images/medium/nn1c03056_m004.gif" alt="" id="_i6"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(4)</span></div></div></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq5"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056/asset/images/medium/nn1c03056_m005.gif" alt="" id="_i7"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(5)</span></div></div></span></div><div class="NLM_p">The Na<sup>+</sup> storage mechanism of In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub> is analogous to that of In<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> due to the similar electrochemical properties of S and Se. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref26" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref26" aria-label="reference 26">(26)</a> Therefore, the electrochemical process of In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub> consists of intercalation, conversion, and alloying/dealloying reactions, as shown below:<span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq6"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056/asset/images/medium/nn1c03056_m006.gif" alt="" id="_i8"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(6)</span></div></div></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq7"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056/asset/images/medium/nn1c03056_m007.gif" alt="" id="_i9"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(7)</span></div></div></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq8"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056/asset/images/medium/nn1c03056_m008.gif" alt="" id="_i10"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(8)</span></div></div></span></div><div class="NLM_p">As shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>a, the CV curve of In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450 in the first cycle displays two reduction peaks at 1.35 and 0.99 V, which disappear in the subsequent scans and thus possibly correspond to the irreversible intercalation of Na<sup>+</sup> and the formation of a solid electrolyte interphase (SEI). <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref41" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref41" aria-label="reference 41">(41)</a> A sharp peak located at 0.73 V is correlated to the conversion reaction of CoSe and In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub> (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq3" aria-label="eqs 3">eqs </a><a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq3" aria-label="3">3</a> and <a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq7" aria-label="7">7</a>), and the peak displayed at 0.24 V can be attributed to the alloying reaction of In to give Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>In (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq8" aria-label="eq 8">eq </a><a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq8" aria-label="8">8</a>). <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref26" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref26" aria-label="reference 26">(26)</a> In the following anodic scan, the peaks at 0.43, 1.25, and 1.52 V are associated with the dealloying process and formation of In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>. Two adjacent peaks appearing at 1.79 and 1.87 V correspond to the desodiation process of CoSe<sub>2</sub> (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq4" aria-label="eqs 4">eqs </a><a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq4" aria-label="4">4</a> and <a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq5" aria-label="5">5</a>). <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref18" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref18" aria-label="reference 18">(18)</a> Moreover, the 3rd and 5th cycles exhibit well-overlapped CV curves, indicating the high reversibility of these electrochemical reactions. In addition, two new reduction peaks appeared at 1.46 and 1.19 V, which could be attributed to the reaction (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq1" aria-label="eqs 1">eqs </a><a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq1" aria-label="1">1</a> and <a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq2" aria-label="2">2</a>) during discharge. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref41" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref41" aria-label="reference 41">(41)</a> The slight shifts of the peaks in the following cycles could be probably ascribed to the structural reorganization during the repeated Na insertion/deinsertion process. Meanwhile, the two peaks close to 0 V in both anodic and cathodic scans could be ascribed to the intercalation/deintercalation of Na<sup>+</sup> into the carbon layers. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref42 ref43" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref42 ref43" aria-label="reference 42 and 43">(42,43)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">The galvanostatic discharge/charge curves of the 1st, 3rd, and 5th cycles of In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450 at a current density of 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup> are shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>b, the charge/discharge plateaus of which are well matched with the CV results. The discharge and charge capacities of the first cycle are as high as 827.5 and 506.2 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>, respectively, with an initial Coulombic efficiency of 61.2%, and the charge/discharge curves of the 3rd and 5th cycles display no observable difference. A high reversible capacity of 477.4 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> could still be achieved after 100 cycles (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056/suppl_file/nn1c03056_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S8</a>). The cycling performances of as-prepared samples are further compared in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>c, where all of them show quite stable capacities. In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450 delivers the highest reversible capacity of 445.0 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 200 cycles at 0.5 A g<sup>–1</sup>, with a capacity retention ratio of 95.7%. The slight, but noticeable, increase in capacity during the first 20 cycles can be related to the activation process of the active materials. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref25 ref44 ref45" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref25 ref44 ref45" aria-label="reference 25, 44 and 45">(25,44,45)</a> Apparently, In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-400 shows a capacity of 370.2 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 200 cycles, which is lower than that of In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450 but higher than that of pure In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub> (290.6 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>) and CoSe<sub>2</sub> (197.3 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>). Post-mortem SEM measurement was carried out to confirm the integrity of the structure (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056/suppl_file/nn1c03056_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S9</a>). Evidently, the rodlike structure of In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450 could be well maintained with no severe structural collapse after the long-term test, indicating a superior structural stability.</div><div class="NLM_p">The rate performance of these samples was also analyzed at different current rates from 0.1 to 20 A g<sup>–1</sup> (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>d). It is apparent that the In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450 delivers the highest reversible capacities at these current rates among the four samples, and even at the highest current of 20 A g<sup>–1</sup>, a stable capacity of 372 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> could be achieved, suggesting an enhanced high-rate performance. In addition, the capacity quickly recovered to 498.3 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> when the current density dropped to 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>. The corresponding charge/discharge curves demonstrated well-defined voltage platforms with no significant distortion at various rates (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056/suppl_file/nn1c03056_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S10</a>), suggesting a low electrochemical polarization. The long-term cycling stability of In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450 was further performed at high current densities (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>e), and reversible capacities of 297.5 and 205.5 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> can still be maintained even after 2000 cycles at 5 and 10 A g<sup>–1</sup>, respectively. The capacity retention is calculated to be 90.0% at 5 A g<sup>–1</sup>, corresponding to a low capacity decay of only 0.005% per cycle. The comparison of rate performance between In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450 and other reported metal selenides-based electrodes is presented in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>f <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref17 ref18 ref46 ref47 ref48 ref49" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref17 ref18 ref46 ref47 ref48 ref49" aria-label="reference 17, 18 and 46 to 49">(17,18,46−49)</a> and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.1c03056/suppl_file/nn1c03056_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S1</a>, showing the advantageous Na<sup>+</sup> storage properties of our sample, especially at higher current densities.</div><div class="NLM_p"><i>Ex situ</i> XRD tests were carried out to gain more insight into the reaction processes of In<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>/CoSe<sub>2</sub>-450.
